    Fixed¶

    1. 🟢 Undo/redo now re-applies the right action when you switch View Layer between scenes. Regression from the v0.7.7 single-sweep rework. Post-undo, _deferred_cascade_apply (core/vl_lifecycle.py) runs apply_overrides(skip_action=True), so re-resolving the action tier is delegated entirely to _maybe_refire_cascade_snap → apply_vl_switch_unified (the forward switch writes ad.action inside the handle_viewlayer_switch depsgraph handler, which is not an undo-step boundary — Rule #2 — so memfile undo doesn't restore those writes). _maybe_refire_cascade_snap gated the re-fire purely on scene['tks_cascade_token'] == TKS_VL_STATE.last_cascade_token: a per-scene custom prop (rolled back by undo) compared against a single global int (survives undo, shared across every scene/VL). The values collide constantly — each scene has its own counter and all VLs of one scene share one — so the gate false-skipped, no Fast Sweep ran, and objects kept the previous VL's action. Confirmed in the user's takes_for_blender_2026-05-28.log: skipped deferred-cascades show apply_overrides … action=0.0ms with no following Fast Sweep … ASSIGN=N line (e.g. L259710, L259762); the tokens only ever held 0/1. Fix: added _vl_context_changed = bool(_vl_pre_undo) and _vl_pre_undo != (scene.name, view_layer.name) to the gate — _vl_pre_undo (captured in _handle_undo_pre/_handle_redo_pre as the pre-restore active context) is the authoritative per-VL "a switch was crossed" signal, immune to token aliasing; the token compare stays as a fallback. Non-switch undos still skip (the gate's _vl_pre_undo == landed case), so the inline ref-snap can't clobber undo-restored state. Rejected alternatives — per-scene-keyed last_cascade_token dict (misses within-scene VLs that share one counter), per-VL token (bumped on the destination, can't detect that the returned-to source VL needs re-establishing), and always-refire (over-snaps non-switch undos) — documented in doc/troubleshooting/undo_vl_switch_action_not_resolved.md. New regression tests dev/tests/test_undo_vl_refire.py (3): context-change-despite-token-collision re-fires, nothing-crossed stays quiet, raw token crossing still re-fires. Full suite 383 passed (Blender 5.1 headless).

    2. 🟢 Undo no longer snaps objects to the rest pose (follow-up to #1, same session). With #1 making the re-fire fire on every cross-/within-scene undo, the user reported "undo not working" — objects jumped to ref pose on Ctrl+Z. Cause: apply_vl_switch_unified STEP 3 snaps unkeyed props to ref state but bypassed is_snap_suppressed() (the suppress_snap_for_undo(1.0) window the undo handler opens and _revert_unkeyed_to_rest_deferred already honors — its docstring: "ref-state snap can overwrite Blender's undo-restored unkeyed transforms"). Post-restart log showed every re-fire logging Fast Sweep … ASSIGN=0 SNAP=3 (e.g. L267281/L267507/L268695) — 3 undo-restored transforms overwritten per undo (SNAP counts only changed values). Fix in core/vl_switch_fast.py: compute _snap_allowed = _has_ref and not is_snap_suppressed() once (after _has_ref), and gate STEP 3 on if _snap_allowed: instead of if _has_ref:. STEP 2 (action assign) still always runs, so the re-fire restores the action without snapping; forward switches are never inside the suppression window so they snap as before. The earlier "always-refire" failed-approach note in the troubleshooting doc predicted this exact regression. Regression tests added to dev/tests/test_undo_vl_refire.py::TestSnapSuppressedDuringUndo (2): apply_vl_switch_unified snaps a drifted object to ref when not suppressed (baseline), and skips the snap (drift preserved) inside the suppression window. Full suite 385 passed (Blender 5.1 headless).

    3. 🟢 Fixed a hard crash when adding View Layers and copying scenes — dangling dynamic-EnumProperty strings. User crash report (Blender 5.0.1): EXCEPTION_ACCESS_VIOLATION (0xc0000005), fault addr 0x2, stack uiBut::~uiBut → UI_block_update_from_old → UI_block_end_ex → ED_region_header_layout → ED_region_header → ED_region_do_draw, after tks.add_viewlayer ×2 + scene.new(NEW) + scene.new(FULL_COPY). Root cause is the documented bpy.props gotcha: a dynamic EnumProperty(items=cb) whose callback builds identifier/name/desc strings at runtime (obj.name, f-strings, os.listdir, str(handle)) and returns a list nothing retains — Blender keeps raw char* into the PyUnicode buffers, the GC frees them when the list is replaced, and the next UI_block_update_from_old / uiBut::~uiBut dereferences freed memory. Direct trigger: TKS_OT_AddViewLayer.target_scene (operators/misc/ops_menus.py) was items=lambda self, ctx: [(s.name, s.name, "") for s in bpy.data.scenes]; add_viewlayer is REGISTER+UNDO with invoke()→execute(), so the redo panel draws that enum, then FULL_COPY mutated bpy.data.scenes, freeing the strings — the persistent editor header was simply the next block to redraw (heap-wide corruption, hence the varied/innocent-looking backtrace). 13 callbacks shared the pattern; preferences/props/props_preset_storage.py:_get_prefs_file_items and preferences/utils_sound.py:get_sound_file_items had already worked around it locally with global _xxx_cache (prior evidence of the same crash). Fix (3-Strikes centralization): new takes_for_blender/utils/enum_cache.py — retain(items) appends to a bounded deque(maxlen=256) and returns items unchanged (strong ref survives until Blender stops drawing the button; deque bounds memory); @retained_enum decorator wraps (self, context) callbacks and routes their return through retain(). Exported from utils/__init__.py; added to the __init__.py reload list. @retained_enum applied to ops_menus._addvl_target_scene_items (was the trigger lambda, hoisted to a named fn), panels/context/properties.py:get_scene_items, properties/slot_ui.py:get_slot_items, variant_switch/properties.py:_get_product_items + _get_variant_items_for_context, operators/inspector/ops_action_assign.py:_get_action_items, panels/navigation/monitors_debug.py:_get_log_file_items, operators/tags/_tag_group_helpers.py:get_tag_group_items, render_presets/operators.py:get_storage_mode_items, render_presets/properties.py:get_tier_filter_items. Indirect helpers retained at the lambda call site with retain(...): operators/context/groups/ops_hierarchy.py (4 lambdas → _enum_scene_groups / _enum_scene_groups_exclude / _enum_vl_groups), operators/inspector/ops_slot_mgmt.py:target_action, render_presets/operators.py:preset_name. Failed approach (recorded so we don't repeat it): a first retained_enum using a *args wrapper to also cover the 4-arg _enum_vl_groups made the addon fail registration — ValueError: EnumProperty(...): expected 'items' function to take 2 arguments, not 0 (a *args fn reports co_argcount==0); the decorator must keep the literal (self, context) signature, and extra-arg helpers retain at the lambda instead. The two pre-existing global _xxx_cache callbacks were left as-is (already correct). Regression tests dev/tests/test_enum_retention.py (7): retain identity, GC-survival, bounded store, decorator return-value + runtime-string retention + extra-arg call-site pattern, and an integration check that _addvl_target_scene_items self-retains. Full suite 392 passed (Blender 5.1 headless), addon registers clean. See doc/troubleshooting/enum_items_dangling_string_crash.md.

    4. 🟢 Cross-scene undo reliably keeps each View Layer's take assignment. Follow-up to Fixed #1/#2 above — and a regression introduced by #1's _vl_context_changed gate. Post-undo, apply_overrides runs skip_action=True, so the action tier is re-applied only by _maybe_refire_cascade_snap → apply_vl_switch_unified, with _post_undo_ping → _process_fresh_actions as the rebuild path (it renames an object's restored autokey-default action — e.g. CubeAction — to the cascade name and rewrites vl.tks_action). On a cross-scene undo landing on an intermediate snapshot, resolve_cascade(ACTION) returns None, but _maybe_refire_cascade_snap still called apply_vl_switch_unified(target_action=None) — whose STEP-1 unassign cleared the object's autokey-default action (Fast Sweep … UN=1 ASSIGN=0; Pass1b … Cube_MESH 'CubeAction' -> 'None') before the ping fired, so the ping found nothing and the tier stayed empty. It ran at all despite cur_token == prev_token because of the _vl_context_changed re-fire gate from #1. Fix in core/vl_lifecycle.py:_maybe_refire_cascade_snap: if _target_action is None: return — skip the destructive re-fire when nothing resolves, so the ping can rebuild the tier (the pre-0.7.7 behavior). Rest-snap is suppressed during the undo grace window anyway (#2), and the re-fire still runs when an action does resolve (cross-scene undo to a VL whose tier survived). Diagnosed by a controlled comparison: the same .blend run through TMP/takes_for_blender_v0.7.6 (works — zero Cascade-token boundary crossed … re-fired lines on undo, so CubeAction survives for the ping) vs HEAD (the re-fired line clears the action); both traces in the troubleshooting doc. NOTE: the v0.7.7 cascade performance work was ruled out — it doesn't touch the post-undo action path (which uses skip_action=True + apply_vl_switch_unified, perf-untouched); all four perf optimizations remain intact (benchmark p50 2.96 ms on the default scene, action-tier-dominant as documented). Open edge (accepted): if the snapshot action is already cascade-named rather than autokey-default, the ping's _is_autokey_default_action_name gate still rejects it — separate, pre-existing limitation. Regression guard dev/tests/test_undo_vl_refire.py::TestRefireBoundaryDetection::test_no_refire_when_cascade_resolves_none (the two sibling boundary tests updated to assert the re-fire does run when an action resolves). Full suite 408 passed (Blender 5.1 headless); user-confirmed in-app on the same file that failed. See doc/troubleshooting/undo_vl_switch_action_not_resolved.md.

    5. 🟢 CURRENT_VL / "Active Layer Only" dispatch guarded on unsaved files. _dispatch in render_scope.py checks bpy.ops.tks.render_active_vl.poll() and wraps the invoke in try/except, reporting a clean message instead of raising RuntimeError: Operator bpy.ops.tks.render_active_vl.poll() failed, context is incorrect when the file is unsaved or there's no active view layer.

    6. 🟢 Clear Pycache / Reload Addon reachable on an unsaved file. TKS_OT_ClearPycache and TKS_OT_ReloadAddon polled on bpy.data.filepath, disabling both whenever no .blend was saved. Neither touches on-disk .blend data (clear deletes __pycache__ under the addon's own install dir resolved from __file__; reload defers an addon disable+enable rebuilding only runtime/PG state), and the gate was inconsistent with TKS_OT_RebuildCache. Dropped both poll methods (commit d8186cf).

    Tooling¶

    Maintainer-only — the doc/reports/ /stats code-quality dashboard + engine. Not shipped in the add-on zip; no takes_for_blender/ runtime change.

    1. /stats Manual-Map Coverage audit (INFO-04). New doc/reports/engine/parts/info_04_manual_map.py (classify_info_04): AST-extracts WIKI_BASE + MANUAL_MAP from takes_for_blender/utils/manual_map.py (never imported — it imports bpy) and replays Blender's right-click → Online Manual matcher (lowercase rna_id + case-sensitive fnmatchcase, first-match-wins) against every right-clickable element: tks.* operators, TKS_AddonPreferences.* props, tks_* data props on Scene/WindowManager/ViewLayer, and operator redo-panel fields (counted only for REGISTER + non-INTERNAL + non-HIDDEN operators — fixed a 591→183 op-field over-count). Status taxonomy explicit/page/wildcard_home/uncovered. New INFO-04 rule in engine/rules.py; state.py gains MANUAL_MAP_PATH/WIKI_DOCS_PATH + ~20 wire_* metrics; visitor.py collects prefs-prop sites, operator bl_options/hidden props, and panel/menu ui_class_meta; report.py::_wireable_block buckets rows by status with an "Appears in (UI)" breadcrumb, the auto-wired suggestion, and a wiki page/anchor scan (_scan_wiki_pages/_scan_md_anchors, :icon: shortcodes stripped, heading level captured). Dashboard renderManualMapWiring (js/app.js) draws status filter tiles, the breadcrumb column, and a two-level page→section override picker (document-order, level-dashed anchors, per-row clear ✕), exporting picks to data/wire_assignments.json. dev/scripts/apply_wire_assignments.py folds those (override ?? auto-wire) into the AUTO-WIRED marker block of manual_map.py (434 lowercased exact entries). Note: the shipped wiring is already all-lowercase (see 0.7.8 Added #3) — the audit exists to keep it that way (uppercase patterns never match Blender's lowercased rna_id, the original 452-prefs dead-end). Tests: dev/tests/test_manual_map_coverage.py (14) + test_manual_map.py all-lowercase guard.
    2. Paste-to-find smart filter + live "Opens ↗" column. New pure, DOM-free doc/reports/js/wire_query.js. wireNormalizeQuery(raw) extracts the identifier from any Blender copy format: operator match is anchored at ^bpy\.ops\. and stops before (, so a kwarg-embedded bpy.ops.… string value can't hijack it; a path ending in ] → last ["…"] key (raw IDProperty); a path ending in .attr → trailing attribute (registered RNA — prefs/data full paths, datablock subscripts ignored); bare tokens pass through; 512-char cap + linear regexes (no O(n²)/ReDoS). wireFilterByQuery matches exact row-tail first (rna.split('.').pop() === token) so a full command lands on exactly that row — batch_render no longer drags in batch_render_bg, and type no longer substring-matches all 1150 rows — falling back to substring only when no tail matches (partial typing/prefix search preserved). Design was hardened against an adversarial review (workflow) that found fatal v1 bugs: lastIndexOf('bpy.ops.') kwarg hijack, prefs paths normalising to the package name takes_for_blender (→0 hits), and substring over-match (type→736, f→580). dev/tests/test_wire_query.js (50 assertions, all adversarial cases) + real-data check: 416/416 operators and 470/470 prefs each resolve to exactly one row. A non-empty search now bypasses the status chip + cause in draw() (all data/prefs props are status page, hidden by the default wildcard_home tile, which made paste-to-find silently return nothing) — Kind dropdown still applies — with a "searching all statuses (tile filter paused)" note; the search box gained an overlaid clear ✕ and Esc-to-clear (stops propagation only when it clears). New "Opens ↗" column: a live <a target="_blank" rel="noopener"> to p.wiki_base + effective-suffix (the dropdown selection, or the auto-wired page on KEEP), updated on every page/section change and clear.
    3. Refresh-command target fix + Settings consolidation + part-file renames. report.py built the website's Refresh command from os.path.abspath(__file__), so it copied python …/engine/report.py — a module that only defines functions and aborts with ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'engine' when run directly (added a __main__ guard pointing at the entry point). Retargeted the command to os.path.join(REPORTS_DIR, "ast_stats_engine.py"); js/app.js::wireCommands() re-derives it from the repo root (cut at /doc/reports/) so it's correct even when the loaded data holds the old path. A first pass appended --no-tests --no-perf for speed, which blanked the TESTS ("Not run") and SPEED ("Not measured") cards — both passes run headless blender --background, so the flags suppressed them — reverted so the main Refresh runs the full pass; regenerated data/codebase_stats.json/.js (Tests 490 passed/1 failed, Speed totals.overall_score 9.9). Refresh + a new clipboard-command Rewire button (copies the apply_wire_assignments.py command) moved into the #settings-popover; .layout-save/.layout-restore added to the shared popover-button selectors (they were falling back to the boxed UA default). Internal refactor: legacy doc/reports/engine/parts/part_*.py renamed to ID-prefixed filenames (part_s→crash_06_restricted_context, part_t→reg_01_class_registration, part_x→corr_04_unreachable, … info_04_manual_map); symbol names (classify_part_*) kept; imports rewired in report.py/cli.py/ast_stats_engine.py. New js/wire_query.js loaded before app.js in index.html.

    [0.7.7] - 2026-05-27¶

    Added¶

    1. Link-and-Assign confirmation when picking a camera that's missing from some scenes. New TKS_OT_LinkCameraAndAssign operator in takes_for_blender/operators/cascade/ops_link_camera.py, registered via the canonical panels/context/_class_registry.py:classes chain (added in the same release after the dead-list trap below — see #5 under Fixed). The picker_menu (TKS_MT_CascadePicker.draw in operators/cascade/_picker.py) now checks each camera item against the tier's covered scenes (bpy.data.scenes for GLOBAL, [bpy.data.scenes.get(m.scene_name) for m in sg.members] for SG); incompatible items get icon='ERROR' + a (missing in N scene(s)) text suffix and route through tks.link_camera_and_assign instead of tks.set_cascade_prop. The operator's invoke() opens wm.invoke_popup(width=380) rendering a 3-button row driven by a mode: EnumProperty(items=[('PROMPT', …), ('LINK', …), ('ASSIGN', …), ('CANCEL', …)]) — the buttons chain back into the same op with a non-PROMPT mode so execute() can branch without a separate operator per action. LINK calls _link_camera_into_scenes(cam, target_scenes) in operators/cascade/_helpers.py which finds cam.users_collection[0] (the camera's "home" collection) and scene.collection.children.link(home_coll) for each target scene — preserving the user's existing collection structure rather than dropping the camera into the master root (per explicit user constraint). Falls back to scene.collection.objects.link(cam) if home_coll is itself a scene's master collection (RuntimeError on the children.link). Both LINK and ASSIGN then chain into bpy.ops.tks.set_cascade_prop() to apply the assignment.

    Changed¶

    1. Camera picker dropdowns now match each tier's reach. Two coordinated changes in takes_for_blender/operators/cascade/:
    2. Scene-bound tiers (Scene / VL / VLG / VLV) — camera_prop_search in _helpers.py:8 gained an optional scene=None kwarg; when provided, cam_col is populated from scene.objects instead of bpy.data.objects. Callers updated: ops_camera_levels.py:467 (Scene), ops_viewlayer_camera.py:118 (VL), ops_camera_levels.py:222-224 (SG popover — now passes g.member_scenes for the multi-scene warning). The generic popover_draw helper (_helpers.py:307) resolves cam_scene = bpy.data.scenes.get(scene_name) if tier in ('SCENE', 'VL', 'VLG', 'VLV') else None and forwards. Global popover at ops_camera_levels.py:83 intentionally passes no scene= so it lists every camera.

    3. Cross-scene tiers (Global / SG) — _camera_collection_fn in _picker.py:27 returns the full list, but TKS_MT_CascadePicker.draw (_picker.py:120) now computes covered_scenes (all scenes for GLOBAL, sg.members scenes for SG) and, per item, calls a new _scenes_missing_camera(cam_name, scenes) helper from _helpers.py. Items with non-empty missing lists get the route-to-link-prompt treatment (see Added #1) plus a visual mark. New _warn_camera_not_in_all_scenes(layout, cam_name, scenes) renders an icon='ERROR' label under the dropdown listing up to 3 missing scenes (then +N more).

    4. Global and Scene Group camera assignments survive scene switches. The auto-clear branch in core/cascade.py:507-557 previously walked back to whichever tier set the cascade and setattr(_owner, _prop, "") when the active scene couldn't resolve to the camera (camera.name not in scene.objects). For Global / SG sources this wiped the assignment for every scene the tier covers, the moment the active scene happened to be one without the camera linked. Pre-fix repro: set master_scene.tks_global_camera = "cam_master" (cam_master linked in Scene A only), switch to Scene B → global wiped, switch back to Scene A → cascade resolves to nothing. Fixed by branching on source: Global / Scene Group → logger.debug(...) + skip applying scene.camera, preserve the tier assignment; Scene / VL / VLG / VLV → auto-clear as before (those tiers are scene-bound, so stale picks are genuinely self-heal-able). The picker UI now warns up-front and offers LINK & ASSIGN (see Added #1), so this branch only fires for stale data from older .blend files or external script writes. See doc/troubleshooting/camera_picker_unfiltered_dropdown.md.

    Fixed¶

    1. Output, View Layer, and File Output standalone preset panels now appear in the Properties tab. TKS_PT_OutputPresetsStandalone, TKS_PT_ViewLayerPresetsStandalone, TKS_PT_FileOutputPresetsStandalone were declared in features/render_presets/panels_ui.py:304-340 and imported at features/render_presets/panels.py:50 but the classes = (...) tuple at L58-80 only contained TKS_PT_RenderPresetsStandalone, TKS_PT_WorldPresetsStandalone, TKS_PT_MaterialPresetsStandalone. The v0.7.5 fix for the same bug class (changelog #3 — "Render preset row visible in Render properties tab on every render engine") patched only the Render standalone; this commit adds the three siblings. Surfaced by the new Part T (Class Registration Coverage) audit which set-diffs declared Blender-base classes against the union of all *classes list members + direct register_class() calls anywhere in the codebase.

    2. Blender no longer prints a flood of _RestrictContext errors at startup. Same root cause across three files:

    3. features/sync/handlers_viewport.py:105 (_propagate_tool_settings) and :130 (_propagate_orientation) read scene = bpy.context.scene directly. The subsequent if scene is None: return guard couldn't help because the attribute access itself raised before the None check could execute. Switched both to scene = getattr(bpy.context, 'scene', None).
    4. utils/pinned.py:39 (_scene_name) previously did return bpy.context.scene.name if bpy.context and bpy.context.scene else "" — the truthy-gate dereferenced .scene before the truthiness check could short-circuit. Rewritten to scene = getattr(bpy.context, 'scene', None); return scene.name if scene else "".

    5. preferences/props/props_sync_viewport.py:23 had a misleading comment claiming _on_sync_toggle "only runs when the user actually toggles" — false, Blender invokes the callback during userpref restore for every prop whose stored value differs from default. Corrected to explicitly document the pref-load invocation path and the downstream getattr guards. Trigger: 10 BoolProperty(update=_on_sync_toggle) bindings on ViewportSyncPropsMixin fire during userpref restore at addon-enable time; the callback chain reaches the two _propagate_* functions which then raised AttributeError: '_RestrictContext' object has no attribute 'scene' — once per non-default toggle on every fresh Blender launch. See doc/troubleshooting/restricted_context_callback_chain.md.

    6. Pytest test runner no longer emits 244 caught fatal exceptions per run. Pytest's _pytest.runner._update_current_test_var writes / pops PYTEST_CURRENT_TEST in os.environ around every test. The teardown pop goes through os.environ.__delitem__ → os.unsetenv() → the Win32 environment API. In Blender's embedded CPython on Windows that path SEGV's — fires once per test teardown (244 access violations in a 375-test run on this machine). Blender's faulthandler catches each SEGV at the C level; pytest is unaware and the test "passes" cleanly. Pre-fix the /stats Tests KPI tile flagged this as Crashed · 2 runner errors (under-counted — engine stopped at the first marker). Patched dev/tests/run_tests.py to monkey-patch _pyt_runner._update_current_test_var = lambda *a, **k: None before pytest.main(). No addon code reads PYTEST_CURRENT_TEST (the tests use pytest fixtures for that), so suppressing the env update has zero cost. Verified: 244 SEGVs → 0. See doc/troubleshooting/pytest_current_test_env_segfault.md, which supersedes the earlier (wrong) order-dependent-state-corruption hypothesis in doc/troubleshooting/test_runner_soft_crash_order_dependent.md.

    7. _clear_actions_on_watched no longer label-walks every sub-target. SPEED audit (dev/scripts/perf_capture.py) flagged cascade_per_prop_ms[action] = 17.6 ms on the default-cube scene — 96 % of total cascade time. cProfile breakdown: 1.9k calls to naming_utils.generate_slot_name per cascade, each doing a bpy.context.preferences.addons.get(...) lookup + RNA attr read + template substitution (~1.5-2 ms each). The labels weren't being consumed — _clear_actions_on_watched in core/cascade_actions.py was iterating iter_anim_targets(obj) (yields (target, slot_label) tuples) purely to null .animation_data.action. Fix in core/vl_targets.py: new iter_anim_targets_only(id_data) mirrors iter_anim_targets's target-enumeration shape (same Object / Scene / World / Material / fallback branches, same dedupe rules for material id() and geometry-nodes node_group id()) but yields just the target ID with no label generation; helper _iter_node_groups_only mirrors _iter_node_groups the same way. Re-exported via core/vl_persistence.py:60 so the existing import path still works. _clear_actions_on_watched switched to the new iterator; the dead if not bpy.data.worlds: return; world = bpy.data.worlds[0] (world variable never referenced) was deleted; the per-iteration from ..utils.pinned import is_pinned was hoisted out of the inner loop; the four duplicated try: apply_rest_values(...) except (RuntimeError, ReferenceError): pass blocks were consolidated into a nested _apply_ref_safely(t) helper that short-circuits when rest_action is None. Measured: factory-startup scene (3 objs, no Rest Action) 14-18 ms → 0.047 ms p50 (~ 380× faster on the no-reference path). Caveat: user scene with 84 objs + Rest Action set stays at 14.9 ms — the residual hot path is apply_rest_values being called twice per sub-target with rest_slot_map rebuilt from scratch on every call (1.8k calls · 22 ms / 10 iter = 92 % of total). That's tracked separately as Fix 6 in doc/troubleshooting/cascade_action_clear_slow.md and deferred to a future commit so the semantics of rest-state snap-back stay untouched in this release.

    8. Undo/redo safety verified with dev/scripts/verify_undo_clear_path.py (assign → undo → null, redo → restored, action.use_fake_user preserved across 5 cycles, _clear_actions_on_watched(scene, vl) no-crash under forced TKS_VL_STATE.is_undoing = True — _apply_ref_safely correctly relies on apply_rest_values's pre-existing is_undoing/is_redoing/is_snap_suppressed() guard at features/rest_state/logic.py:38-52 to skip the ref-snap during undo grace) plus the full dev/tests/test_undo_safety.py suite (8 tests covering basic undo/redo, undo-after-action-creation, multiple-cycle stability, pointer stability, history jump, fake-user-survives-undo).

    9. Companion fix in core/vl_handlers.py:unregister() — the dead-register cleanup (entry #5 below) removed the empty classes = [] scaffold from vl_handlers.py, but the matching for cls in reversed(classes): unregister_class(cls) loop in unregister() was left behind referencing the deleted variable. Surfaced via [TKS INFO] [CORE:INIT] Failed to unregister takes_for_blender.core.vl_persistence: name 'classes' is not defined log line on every addon disable. Loop removed; no classes were ever registered from this file so no actual unregister logic was lost. Audit-engine test runs that disable/enable repeatedly went from 202 / 375 passed (345 ERROR rows from the dangling unregister) back to clean 375 / 375.
    10. Companion micro-fix in core/naming_utils.py — get_addon_prefs() now caches the prefs lookup result in a module-level _cached_prefs. The cache is invalidated explicitly via reset_addon_prefs_cache() wired into takes_for_blender/__init__.py:unregister() so addon-disable/enable cycles still resolve the new prefs instance. Pre-fix _build_token_values (called from generate_slot_name 1.9k times per cascade) re-resolved bpy.context.preferences.addons.get(ADDON_MODULE) each call. After Fix 1 the call frequency dropped enough that this cache contributes less than half a millisecond on its own, but it's the right shape going forward.
    11. Fix 6 (the deferred rest-state residual): apply_rest_values gained optional rest_slot_map= / rest_slot_map_short= kwargs (built once via new build_rest_slot_map(rest_action) helper) so the per-call rebuild is skipped; _clear_actions_on_watched pre-builds the maps once and drops the redundant per-sub-target _apply_ref_safely call (apply_rest_values(obj) already walks iter_anim_targets(obj) and snaps every sub-target). Also gated the per-call tks_log behind tks_log_active('CORE','REST'). User scene 14.9 → 9.7 ms p50 (SPEED 5.7 → 8.0). A lazy-label variant was prototyped and reverted (10.07 → 10.45 ms — most slots are template-named, so the lazy path always fell through to generate the label anyway).
    12. Fix v3 (core/naming_utils.py): session-scoped generate_name cache keyed by (template_key, separator, effective_kwargs), where _resolve_context_tokens pre-bakes every implicit context-derived token (scene / viewlayer / world / object / type / action / material / collection / parent) into the key so a context shift can't return a stale hit. _generate_name_uncached kept as a bypass escape hatch. Invalidation via reset_label_cache() from _autosave_preferences (covers template + separator edits) and reset_addon_prefs_cache. Rename safety is automatic (the new name flows into the key). 100 % hit rate post-warmup (dev/scripts/probe_label_cache.py); cache safety proven across all 6 context tokens (dev/scripts/verify_label_cache_safety.py). Plus a cached _log_ref flag in apply_rest_values replacing 4 per-FCurve tks_log_active checks. User scene 9.7 → 8.6 ms p50 (SPEED 8.0 → 8.4).

    13. Fix v4 (the big one — features/rest_state/logic.py + core/cascade_actions.py): extracted _resolve_rest_slot() (exact-key → template-label → raw-name → id-prefix substring fallback) and _snap_one_target() (per-target FCurve snap) from apply_rest_values so the per-object path and the cascade-clear path share one implementation. Rewrote _clear_actions_on_watched as a single labeled walk (was two walks: label-less clear + labeled snap) that resolves the slot inline and snaps only on a hit, with the undo-guard / mirror-suppress / slot-map build / log-active read hoisted to once-per-cascade-pass. A dev/scripts/probe_rest_snap_breakdown.py measurement showed only 1 of 84 objects (1.2 %) actually has a matching ref slot, so the second walk + per-call setup was ~99 % wasted. User scene 8.6 → 2.7 ms p50 (SPEED 8.4 → 9.9 🟢, cumulative 18.65 → 2.73 ms, −85 %). False-negative trap (an object matching only via the substring fallback being wrongly skipped) is avoided by resolving the slot for every target with the shared helper — no separate coverage heuristic. Locked down by new dev/tests/test_rest_state.py::TestClearActionsSnap (4 characterization cases: exact-name, no-match-untouched, substring-fallback, no-ref-action) that pass identically before and after the refactor. Full progression + the deferred Fix v4-followup levers documented in doc/troubleshooting/cascade_action_clear_slow.md.

    14. Internal: 8 dead register() functions removed across the addon; 2 orphaned operators routed to canonical registration. panels/popovers/__init__.py declared a 91-class classes = list(_cascade_classes) + list(_misc_classes) list + register() / unregister() pair that nobody called — panels/__init__.py:modules doesn't include popovers and no other module imports popovers.register. All 91 classes ARE registered, but via panels/context/_class_registry.py:classes (the canonical chain consumed by panels.context.register()). The dead infrastructure was a footgun: adding a class there appeared to work (no errors at import time) but the operator silently never registered. This trap caught TKS_OT_LinkCameraAndAssign when it was first added during the v0.7.7 work; layout.operator("tks.link_camera_and_assign", ...) returned None on every picker click and the next attribute assignment raised AttributeError: 'NoneType' object has no attribute 'camera_name'. Cleanups:

    15. panels/popovers/__init__.py — deleted _cascade_classes, _misc_classes, classes, register(), unregister(), plus the orphan TKS_CamFilterItem class (the matching WindowManager.tks_cam_filtered CollectionProperty went away too; camera_prop_search falls back to tks_scene_cameras which is registered via the canonical chain).
    16. operators/context/ops_crud.py — deleted dead classes list + register() / unregister() (all 9 classes — TKS_OT_DeleteScene, TKS_OT_ToggleSceneRender, etc. — canonical-registered via _class_registry.py).
    17. panels/inspector/popovers.py — deleted dead classes list + register() / unregister() (all 7 classes — TKS_OT_ObjectActionPopover, TKS_OT_ObjectSlotPopover, etc. — canonical-registered via operators/inspector/ops_popovers.py).
    18. operators/cascade/ops_link_camera.py — initial commit included a dead register() / unregister() per template; removed for the same reason.

    20. Reachability sentinels for two false positives Part T can't model yet (the from .X import register re-export pattern): core/vl_handlers.py (# REGISTER_OK: re-exported via vl_persistence.py:60 + deleted the empty classes = [] scaffold) and panels/context_render_queue.py (# REGISTER_OK: re-exported as _rq_register via panels/context/__init__.py:345). The engine's classify_part_t was extended to scan the 6 lines above each def register(): for # REGISTER_OK: and route matches into t_exempt instead of t_dead_register.

    21. Internal: three new static-analysis audit Parts on the /stats dashboard + a headless Speed Benchmark gauge.

    22. Part S — Restricted-Context Safety (catches the bug class behind Fixed #2 above). New classify_part_s post-walk classifier in ~/.claude/skills/blender-code-quality/scripts/ast_stats_engine.py. Enumerates restricted-context entry points (*Property(update=…), bpy.app.handlers.<load_pre|load_post|save_pre|save_post>.append(…), bpy.app.timers.register(…, first_interval=0|persistent=True)) and walks each callback's call graph up to 2 hops deep, flagging unguarded bpy.context.<attr> reads. Safe-attrs whitelist: {preferences, window_manager}. Sentinel: # RESTRICT_OK: <reason> within 3 lines above the read. Detector validated against 12 standalone fixtures under dev/tests/fixtures/restricted_context_bugs/ (6 bad, 5 ok, 1 exempt) wired into dev/tests/test_part_s_restricted_context.py which loads the engine via importlib.util.spec_from_file_location and asserts per-fixture expected critical/exempt counts plus the 2-hop chain detection that matches the production bug shape.
    23. Part T — Class Registration Coverage (catches the bug class behind Fixed #1 + #5 above). Three sub-checks: declared-but-not-registered, dead register() (function unreachable from the addon root's master register() via the import + mod.register() call graph), and same-class-in-2+-live-lists. Live audit on the codebase pre-cleanup: 3 critical unregistered Panels (the Output/ViewLayer/FileOutput siblings) + 6 dead register() functions (including the 91-class popovers list) + 137 false-positive duplicates (mostly the popovers↔registry overlap because popovers was dead). Post-fix: 0 / 0 / 0 + 1 exempt (the documented vl_handlers.register re-export). Reachability graph follows for m in modules: m.register() patterns by reading the modules = [...] list literal at module scope; uses bare-name resolution for cross-file from .X import classes import chains. Duplicate-list check filters to "≥ 2 lists each iterated by a reachable register()" so the popovers-vs-registry overlaps don't pollute the count when one side is dead.

    24. SPEED — Headless Speed Benchmark. New dev/scripts/perf_capture.py runs in Blender headless, disables/re-enables the addon to time the cold register cycle, counts TKS_* classes registered (proxy for cold-start cost), and runs apply_overrides 10 times (with 2-sample warmup) for p50/p95 plus a per-prop breakdown via apply_overrides(..., prop_filter=CascadeProperty.X) for camera/world/compositor/action/presets individually. Prints JSON between sentinels for the audit engine to scrape. Sub-scores 0-10: addon_enable_ms (10 @ <=500ms, 0 @ >=2000ms), cascade_apply_p50_ms (10 @ <=2ms, 0 @ >=20ms), cascade_apply_p95_ms (10 @ <=5ms, 0 @ >=50ms). Overall is the mean. Informational only — does NOT deduct from Code Quality. Engine's _build_speed_part builds a recommendations list per slow measurement attributing the slowness to a specific code area (e.g. "p50 17.8 ms · dominated by action cascade (17.6 ms = 96 % of cascade time)" with fix-target pointing at core/cascade_actions.py + core/cascade.py (action branch ~L663-768)). Full audit of the dominant action-cascade hotspot at doc/troubleshooting/cascade_action_clear_slow.md.

Engine's run_tests was rewritten to parse every fault (not just the first), classify each by stack frame (addon vs infrastructure based on whether takes_for_blender/ appears in the trace), collapse identical infrastructure faults into a single [infrastructure ×N] row, and emit synthetic __runner_mode__:… + __fault_summary__:… meta rows that the JSON builder converts into top-level fields.

    [0.7.6] - 2026-05-27¶

    Added¶

    1. Rest State sub-panel under Globals re-wired into the register chain. TKS_PT_RestState (features/rest_state/panels.py) — a bl_parent_id='TKS_PT_Globals', bl_options={'DEFAULT_CLOSED'} sub-panel exposing wm.tks_rest_action via prop_search and a static info box ("Unkeyed properties will snap to values from Rest Action.") — had existed since the 0.5.x era but was never being registered. features/rest_state/__init__.py now imports from . import panels and calls panels.register() / panels.unregister() in matched order. draw_header toggles a GHOST_ENABLED/GHOST_DISABLED icon based on whether tks_rest_action is bound. NOTE: the existing poll() gates on prefs.preferences.active_tab == 'GLOBALS', which is not in the current active_tab enum (WORKFLOW/UI/DATA/DEBUG) — so visibility currently relies on Blender's parent-panel propagation rather than the poll filter. Worth a follow-up audit but the user-visible effect (panel renders inside the Globals tab of the N-panel) is correct.

    Changed¶

    1. Rule tag preset rows now render with the same stacked layout as the Globals → Presets overview. _draw_rule_presets in takes_for_blender/panels/tag_library_ui/draw.py previously rendered each per-category preset field (render_preset, output_preset, fileoutput_preset, viewlayer_preset, colormanagement_preset for OUTPUT; camera_preset for CAMERA; world_preset for STUDIO; material_preset for MATERIAL) as a single split(factor=0.35) row — label on the left, [tks.search_render_preset] [tks.unlink_tag_preset] on the right — so the user could see the assigned preset name but had no way to switch which storage tier the search popup was browsing, no visual cue for where the currently-assigned preset lived, and the visual treatment diverged from the regular preset rows. Rewrote the loop to mirror the globals_panel.py::TKS_PT_Globals.draw PRESETS-mode pattern (lbl = col.row(); lbl.active = False; lbl.label(...); styles.preset_row(col, …)): for each field draw a dimmed col.row() with active = False carrying the category label + icon, then a col.box().row(align=True) containing four widgets in this order: (1) row.prop(config, f"{preset_type}_tier_filter", text="", icon_only=True) — the same per-type EnumProperty declared on tks_preset_config in features/render_presets/properties.py (render_tier_filter, output_tier_filter, etc.) that _get_search_items in features/render_presets/operators.py already reads to filter the search popup by tier; (2) a fixed-width badge = row.row(); badge.ui_units_x = 1.0; badge.label(text="", icon=tier_icon) cluster where tier_icon is _ser.TIER_ICONS.get(_ser.find_preset_tier(preset_type, current), 'DOT') when a preset is assigned, falling back to 'DOT' on (RuntimeError, AttributeError) or when no preset is currently assigned (so the badge column stays a fixed 1 ui-unit and rows stay vertically aligned); (3) the existing tks.search_render_preset operator, now decorated with the same type-specific button icon (SCENE / OUTPUT / FILE / RENDERLAYERS / IMAGE_RGB_ALPHA / CAMERA_DATA / WORLD / MATERIAL) the regular preset rows use, and text "Select" when unassigned (replacing the previous "--" placeholder); (4) the existing tks.unlink_tag_preset X button, rendered only when a preset is assigned. config = getattr(context.scene, 'tks_preset_config', None) and from ...features.render_presets import serialization as _ser are hoisted before the loop. No + create-menu and no ✓ / ✏️ / ↩ action sub-row is drawn — those are scene-applied-preset semantics (save / edit / revert against tks_preset_config) and don't apply to a rule-tag pointer. No data-model changes: the filter dropdown writes to the same scene-level tks_preset_config.<type>_tier_filter enum the main preset row uses, so changing the tier filter from the rule UI also re-filters subsequent searches in the regular preset rows (intentional: one Storage filter per type, addon-wide).

    Fixed¶

    1. Three dead migration-banner buttons removed from the context panel header. panels/context/panel.py:38-53 had two banner blocks gated on wm.tks_migration_message / wm.tks_pending_migrations containing three layout.operator(...) calls — tks.dismiss_migration_message, tks.run_all_migrations, tks.dismiss_all_migrations — none of which were declared as the bl_idname of any operator in the addon. The Part R Unknown-Panel-Operator check (added in this same release) caught all three. Static cross-reference confirmed the WindowManager properties driving the banner were never written to anywhere in the addon, so the banner was unreachable under normal use but would have crashed if any external script set either prop. Removed the banner render blocks AND the matching bpy.types.WindowManager.tks_migration_message / tks_pending_migrations StringProperty / IntProperty declarations in panels/inspector/__init__.py:386-395 plus their cleanup entries in the unregister props list. Future migration system can re-introduce a fresh surface.
    2. Cache-Rebuild operator hardened across three Code-Quality audit flags.
    3. Missing poll() (Part D) — TKS_OT_RebuildCache had no poll. Added a @classmethod poll(cls, context) returning context.window_manager is not None. The rebuild operates on in-memory addon state + a per-scene IDProperty stamp, both of which exist as long as Blender is running, so any real context qualifies.
    4. Debug print() (Part D) — print(f"[TKS] Addon reload failed: {e}") at the deferred-reload failure path replaced with a defensive double-try tks_log(level='ERROR', topic='CORE', subtopic='reload'). The outer try absorbs the case where tks_log itself can't be imported mid-reload.
    5. Unregistered Persistent Procs (Part I) — core/cache_version.py::_stamp_on_save and _check_on_load (registered via bpy.app.handlers.save_pre / load_post) were never registered with the addon's Process Monitor. Added matched register_process("Cache Version Stamp" / "Cache Version Check", HANDLER, CORE, ...) calls + unregister_process pairs.
    6. _reload_addon reload timer lifted to module scope with defensive double-fire guard. Was defined as a closure inside TKS_OT_RebuildCache.execute(), so each rebuild click produced a fresh reference and bpy.app.timers.unregister(_reload_addon) had no stable target. The closed-over addon_module is now carried via a single-slot module-level _PENDING_RELOAD_MODULE which execute() sets immediately before if bpy.app.timers.is_registered(_reload_addon): bpy.app.timers.unregister(_reload_addon) → register(_reload_addon, first_interval=0.1). Net effects: (a) Part O Reload-Race Timers reclassified from 🟠 at-risk to ✅ safe (Footprint score 9.95 → 10.0); (b) genuine double-click race resolved — Blender previously raised RuntimeError: timer already registered on a second rebuild click within the 100 ms window. Added a K5_EXEMPT: sentinel at the schedule site with a justification (the body's bpy.ops.preferences.addon_disable/enable doesn't touch addon-managed undo-tracked state, so an is_undoing guard would be a no-op).
    7. The keymap-audit monitor no longer ticks in the background when debug logging is off. _periodic_tick in takes_for_blender/utils/keymap_audit.py was unconditionally calling snapshot_user_kc() — which walks both wm.keyconfigs.user and wm.keyconfigs.addon, filtering every kmi by is_user_defined and the addon's tks.* / wm.call_menu_pie namespace — on every fire of the persistent 2.5 s timer registered at module load. Only the tks_log(topic="UI", subtopic="HOTKEYS") output was gated by enable_debug_logging + log_topic_ui; the snapshot/diff work itself was always running, contradicting the section header's "Disabled by default to keep idle CPU near zero" promise. Added _audit_logging_enabled() that delegates to the existing tks_log_active(topic="UI", subtopic="HOTKEYS") pre-check helper (takes_for_blender/utils/logger.py:192), and short-circuited _periodic_tick to return _PERIODIC_TICK_SECONDS immediately when the helper returns False, clearing _periodic_last_snapshot so a later re-enable starts from a fresh baseline instead of diffing against a stale snapshot captured before disable. The timer stays registered, so toggling enable_debug_logging or log_topic_ui at runtime takes effect on the next tick — no addon reload required. The unconditional register_periodic_tick() call in takes_for_blender/__init__.py:312 is unchanged; the gate is internal, with a comment explaining the design choice for future readers.
    8. Stats engine extended with Part R (Operator Dispatcher Audit) and Part W (Wiki Health), plus ROOT auto-detect.
    9. Part R: nine static-AST sub-checks over every Operator / Panel / Menu subclass — self-recursion, unknown tks.* dispatch target, unknown panel.operator(...) string, missing / duplicate bl_idname, empty / pass-only execute() body, bare return or return None inside execute (top-level only, not nested helpers), poll() missing @classmethod, op.<attr> = ... writes to undeclared bpy.props.* on the target operator. Sentinel # DISPATCH_OK: <reason> exempts deliberate same-id dispatches. Deduction weights: 0.5 per critical, 0.1 per warning. Caught both 0.7.5 button-op crashes (tks.tag_add_new, tks.delete_tag_item) plus the three dead migration buttons in #1 above. Lives under ~/.claude/skills/blender-code-quality/scripts/ast_stats_engine.py (engine implementation) — surfaced into quality.checks, parts.R.totals, parts.R.rows, the markdown report's ## Part R - Operator Dispatcher Audit section, and the HTML dashboard via HUMAN_CONTENT.R (icon alert_triangle, status callback aggregates crash-class vs silent-fail counts).
    10. Part W: read-only view of the persistent wiki-drift ledger at doc/reports/other/wiki_open_todos.json. The engine doesn't re-run the wiki scan itself (wiki lives in a sibling repo and may not be present on every machine) — it surfaces whatever the ledger says so the dashboard always shows the latest known state. parts.W.totals exposes open/closed/ignored + severity breakdown. Informational only; doesn't deduct from any score.
    11. ROOT auto-detect: the engine's ROOT was hardcoded to ~/Takes-for-Blender, so on machines where the clone lives elsewhere (e.g. ~/Documents/GitHub/Takes-for-Blender) it silently scanned 0 files and wrote empty reports. New _detect_root() tries $TKS_STATS_ROOT env var → legacy hardcoded path → cwd walk-up for takes_for_blender/blender_manifest.toml → known canonical clone locations under $HOME. Surfaced the actual scan duration (95.7s, 345 files, 406 operators) instead of the previous 0.00s mystery.
    12. HTML dashboard upgrades: per-tile step controls, "View all" popup, file-structure tile on overview, drag-drop restored, layout fixes.
    13. Per-tile step controls (+1 / +2 / 5 / 10 / All / Less) on every breakdown table and bar list, persisted in localStorage under tks-overview-tile-sizes keyed by data-tile-id. Same model maps to row count for tables and to max-height (in line-heights) for the file tree. +1 / +2 are relative; 5 / 10 are absolute (set-to-N) and only render when distinct from the current count.
    14. "View all" popup button — attachStepFooter now accepts a {title, icon, build} callback; clicking opens the existing modal infrastructure with a full uncapped re-render of the dataset. Wired at every call site: renderBreakdownTable, renderBarList, file-tree (overview + Part A drill-in).
    15. File-structure tree now visible on the overview page directly via a new <pre class="file-tree" id="ov-file-structure"> tile in composition-row. Previously only rendered inside Part A's drill-in. Engine now emits composition.file_structure in the JSON payload (was always written to the markdown report but never to JSON — pre.textContent = comp.file_structure; was a no-op when the field stayed "").
    16. Section drag-and-drop restored. .overview-section-drag <button> elements were never set draggable="true" anywhere (HTML buttons are NOT draggable by default), so the dragstart listener's .closest('.overview-section-drag') branch never fired. Mirrored the tile-drag pattern: set the attribute on the handle at render time when _layoutMode is on, and toggle it for all existing handles inside _setLayoutMode.
    17. Excluded Checks card switched from chip-strip rounded pills to a <table class="breakdown-table"> rendered through renderBreakdownTable with {severity: '🟢', severity_label: e.note}. Reads as one consistent visual family with Code Quality / Footprint above it.
    18. Composition card now stacks rows vertically. Two .stat-list rule blocks existed in components.css: the second (line ~1403) overrode the first with display: grid; grid-template-columns: max-content auto; — a dt/dd-style layout only referenced from the legacy legacy/codebase_stats.html mirror — and was silently making the live dashboard's stat-list render pairs side-by-side instead of one-per-row. Panel-draw smoke coverage (dev/tests/test_panel_draw_smoke.py): previously skipped TKS_PT_SmartOutput wholesale via _CONTEXT_RESTRICTED_PANELS because its draw() reads context.active_node.{bl_idname, directory, file_name, file_output_items, name} — context attributes that Blender's UI dispatch guarantees in a NODE_EDITOR space but --background mode does not. Replaced the skip dict with a generic _CONTEXT_BUILDERS dict that maps panel-name → factory returning a context-like wrapper around bpy.context with the required overrides; the TKS_PT_SmartOutput factory synthesises a MagicMock(bl_idname='CompositorNodeOutputFile', name='File Output', directory='', file_name='', file_output_items=[]) and exposes it via a _CtxWrap.__getattr__ proxy that returns bpy.context attributes for everything else.
