    [0.7.5] - 2026-05-22¶

    Added¶

    1. Delete a preset file from disk with Alt+click on the X in any preset row. TKS_OT_SelectPreset gained an invoke() that detects event.alt and not self.preset_name (the X's "unlink" intent). When that branch fires it reads the current preset name from context.scene.tks_preset_config.<type>_preset, decodes the tier-qualified key via serialization.decode_preset_key, and delegates to bpy.ops.tks.delete_render_preset('INVOKE_DEFAULT', preset_type=…, preset_name=bare). TKS_OT_DeleteRenderPreset.invoke already calls context.window_manager.invoke_confirm, so Blender's native confirm dialog appears and on accept the file is removed, preset caches invalidated, and the assigned name cleared from tks_preset_config. Plain click falls through to execute() unchanged. No new operator, no new tooltip string. Files: takes_for_blender/features/render_presets/panels_ui.py.
    2. Folder icons on the Addon and Project preset locations open the folder in your file explorer. Two new INTERNAL operators in takes_for_blender/features/render_presets/operators.py — TKS_OT_OpenAddonPresetsFolder (tks.open_addon_presets_folder) and TKS_OT_OpenProjectPresetsFolder (tks.open_project_presets_folder). Both call serialization._get_addon_presets_dir() / _get_project_presets_dir() and hand the result to the existing utils.open_folder.open_path_in_explorer helper (Windows os.startfile / macOS open / Linux xdg-open). The Project operator has a poll() that returns bool(serialization._get_project_presets_dir()), so the button greys out until the .blend is saved (Project tier lives next to the .blend). Buttons added to preferences/draw_data_storage.py::_draw_storage with icon='FILE_FOLDER', mirroring the existing Shared / Local rows. No browse dialog — plain click only.

    Changed¶

    1. World preset row greys out when scene.world is None, with a hint pointing the user at the next step. Previously the row stayed active but capture_world_settings(scene.world) and apply_world_settings(scene.world, …) both take the world data-block as a positional argument — picking a preset on a worldless scene silently no-op'd. draw_world_preset_header in panels_helpers.py now wraps styles.preset_row in a row = self.layout.row() + row.enabled = has_world shell and follows it with self.layout.box().label(text="Assign a world to use presets", icon='INFO') when no world is present. Mirrors the existing camera pattern (draw_camera_preset_header's is_scene_cam gate). TKS_PT_WorldPresetsStandalone.draw now delegates to the helper instead of calling styles.preset_row itself, so the disabled-state behaviour lives in one place.
    2. Variants list settings menu toggles index numbers and per-row stats, both off by default. Two new BoolProperty annotations on bpy.types.WindowManager registered in features/variant_switch/properties.py, both default=False: tks_vsw_show_index and tks_vsw_show_stats. _draw_index_box(parent, index_value, force_show=False, show_placeholder=True) in features/variant_switch/ui_helpers.py now draws either the boxed number, a dimmed DOT icon inside the same fixed-width column (ui_units_x = IDX_BOX_WIDTH), or nothing at all — the latter when show_placeholder=False and the number is hidden. _draw_state passes show_placeholder=False because state rows already lead with an active-state socket / keyframe-icon column (built from template_node_socket for the active variant, tks.vsw_set_edit_state operator for inactive variants), and a side-by-side dot would carry no extra meaning. _draw_pool_mat passes force_show=True because item.pool_idx is the slot-pool index the variant cascade engine writes against when picking which material to assign — hiding it would lose semantic information, unlike the decorative indices on PRODUCT / STATE / PART / MATERIAL rows. _draw_product and _draw_material wrap their stat clusters (states/parts/mats counts on PRODUCT rows; pool count + object-count walker on MATERIAL rows) in if getattr(wm, 'tks_vsw_show_stats', False): blocks. The separator between stats and the trailing Collection icon moved inside the same gate so the icon stays flush against the row name when stats are hidden. Interactive controls remain unconditional: the STATE activator socket, PART visibility prop-toggles, MATERIAL pool_index field, and every OUTLINER_COLLECTION popover button. TKS_MT_VSW_ProductsSettings.draw in features/variant_switch/panel.py swaps layout.prop(wm, "tks_vsw_show_collection", text="Collection") for two rows — tks_vsw_show_index ("Index Numbers") and tks_vsw_show_stats ("Stats"). The tks_vsw_show_collection property is left in place because the legacy TKS_UL_VSW_Products.draw_item (registered but no longer drawn via template_list) still reads it; removing the WM property without also pruning the dead UIList would crash that UIList if it ever became reachable. Cleanup of the dead UIList stays out of scope for this fix.
    3. Visual gap between the Inspector's function-key icons and the view-mode toggles. _draw_channel_content in panels/inspector/panel.py and draw_channels_full in panels/channels/draw.py both build the same right-aligned icon row: BOOKMARKS → TIME → LONGDISPLAY → LIGHTPROBE_PLANE (the last only in the main panel; the popup variant stops at LONGDISPLAY because it can't exit channels view). Without a divider the four icons read as a single homogeneous group at the rendered density. Added an icon_row.separator(factor=1.0) between the function-key pair (bookmarks / timeline) and the mode-toggle pair (slotted / channels) in both call sites.

    Fixed¶

    1. Color Management presets no longer raise AttributeError: 'CurveMap' object has no attribute 'extend' on apply. Root cause: extend is a property of bpy.types.CurveMapping (the parent struct), not of individual bpy.types.CurveMap rows. _capture_curve_mapping in serialization/capture.py was writing 'extend': getattr(curve, 'extend', 'EXTRAPOLATED') into each per-curve dict — silently returning the default literal because the attribute doesn't exist on CurveMap. _apply_curve_mapping_curves in serialization/apply.py then tried target.extend = extend on a CurveMap, raising AttributeError. The except (TypeError, ValueError) didn't catch it, so the whole apply_colormanagement_settings aborted. Fix: drop the per-curve 'extend' field at both ends. Parent-level extend already round-trips via the scalar view_settings.curve_mapping.extend path captured by the parent attribute loop. Legacy presets carrying the stale per-curve key are silently ignored on apply. See doc/troubleshooting/colormanagement_preset_curvemap_extend.md.
    2. tks.tag_add_new no longer hard-crashes Blender via unbounded Python recursion. TKS_OT_TagAddNew.execute() in operators/tags/ops_groups_query.py was return bpy.ops.tks.tag_add_new('INVOKE_DEFAULT') — calling its own bl_idname. The recursion overflowed Blender's native C stack before a Python RecursionError could surface, so the process simply terminated with no traceback. Git archaeology (git log -G) showed the dispatcher originally pointed at the now-removed tks.roadmap_add_tag (commit 0829e0d); commit f0da905 did a careless text-rename and pointed it at itself. Replaced with a real implementation: get_tag_library(context), ensure_categories(context), resolve target category and group from _resolve_active_tag_item (falling back to lib.active_category), pick a unique "New Tag[.NNN]" against both cat.tags and every group.tags, target_collection.add() + _prev_name stamp to suppress the _on_tag_renamed propagation handler on creation, then sync_tag_tree(context) and select the new row in wm.tks_tag_tree_index. See doc/troubleshooting/tag_add_new_self_recursion_crash.md.
    3. Render preset row is now visible in the Render properties tab regardless of render engine. panels.py was prepending draw_render_preset_header to CYCLES_RENDER_PT_sampling — a Cycles-only sub-panel that only exists when the Cycles addon is loaded, and that even then sits inside the default-collapsed Sampling section. Architecture spec at doc/architecture/core_logic_patterns.md §16.6.1 already required a standalone fallback panel for this exact case, and TKS_PT_RenderPresetsStandalone (bl_context='render', bl_order=-1, HIDE_HEADER, empty bl_label) was written for that purpose but was imported and never added to the classes tuple. Sibling TKS_PT_WorldPresetsStandalone / TKS_PT_MaterialPresetsStandalone follow the same pattern and are registered — that's why those tabs always worked. Fix: register TKS_PT_RenderPresetsStandalone, drop the CYCLES_RENDER_PT_sampling prepend. See doc/troubleshooting/render_preset_row_invisible_in_properties.md.
    4. Color Management → Working Space → File now applies from a saved preset. Capture was correct (the JSON contained "blend_data.colorspace.working_space": "<value>", verified against a user preset). Apply silently failed: bpy.ops.wm.set_working_color_space(working_space=value) either no longer resolves under that name in Blender 5.1 (the AttributeError was swallowed by the bare except), or it returns {'CANCELLED'} without raising — in which case the old code returned True while the dropdown stayed unchanged. After the operator branch the fall-through _set_property(blend_cs, 'working_space', value) hits the prop's is_readonly flag and fails silently too. Rewrote _set_blend_colorspace_property with a layered, verified strategy: (1) direct setattr(blend_cs, 'working_space', value) followed by a read-back compare; (2) operator candidates (set_working_color_space, 'working_space'), (set_working_colorspace, 'working_space'), (set_working_color_space, 'colorspace') looked up via getattr(bpy.ops.wm, name, None), each call followed by a read-back compare so a {'CANCELLED'} return can't fake success; (3) tks_log(topic="PRESET", subtopic="colormanagement") line per failed attempt so the next regression isn't silent. See doc/troubleshooting/working_space_file_apply_silent_failure.md.
    5. Drop & Re-apply preset mode no longer floods bpy.ops.tks.revert_all_presets() every ~0.2 s. Root cause: panels/navigation/panel.py::draw() was calling schedule_preset_automation('DROP_REAPPLY') whenever dirty_types was non-empty. The _preset_auto_pending guard correctly suppressed re-scheduling within the same 0.2 s window, but as soon as the deferred timer fired and cleared the guard, the next draw() (which runs on every redraw — mouse move, frame change, …) saw dirty_types still non-empty and re-scheduled. Net: revert_all_presets ran roughly every 0.2 s as long as the panel was visible. Fix: move DROP_REAPPLY off the draw trigger and onto the event bus. Added _on_vl_switch_post_drop_reapply subscriber in panels/navigation/logic.py and register_drop_reapply_handler / unregister_drop_reapply_handler wired through panels/navigation/__init__.py::register(). The subscriber listens on core.event_bus.VL_SWITCH_POST_CASCADE (already emitted from core/vl_switch.py after each VL change applies its cascade tiers), reads preset_change_mode from prefs, and schedules 'DROP_REAPPLY' only when the active mode matches. panel.py::draw() keeps the ALWAYS_SYNC branch because its documented intent is genuinely continuous. Architectural rule enforced: bpy.ops calls never originate from draw(). See doc/troubleshooting/drop_reapply_flood_per_redraw.md.
    6. Switching the Inspector to Channels view actually shows the channels. TKS_OT_ToggleInspectorMode.invoke in operators/inspector/ops_inspector_misc.py flipped wm.tks_inspector_show_channels between True/False but never touched the sub-mode enum wm.tks_channel_mode (default 'SLOTTED'). _draw_channel_content in panels/inspector/panel.py:116 reads tks_channel_mode and branches: 'CHANNELS' draws panels/channels/draw.draw_channels, anything else draws the Scene / World / Object slotted sections. Net: clicking the LIGHTPROBE_PLANE channels-view button entered the channel-view container but stayed on the slotted layout the user had left it on. Fix: when the operator turns tks_inspector_show_channels ON for self.mode == 'CHANNELS', also force wm.tks_channel_mode = 'CHANNELS'. Toggling channels view OFF is unchanged — the sub-mode is preserved so a later re-enter doesn't override an explicit tks.toggle_channel_mode flip the user might have made.
    7. tks.delete_tag_item no longer hard-crashes Blender via unbounded Python recursion. Same bug pattern as Fixed #2 (tks.tag_add_new): commit f0da905 did a careless text-rename and pointed the single-tag delete dispatcher in TKS_OT_DeleteTagItem.execute (operators/tags/ops_groups_query.py:262) at the operator's own bl_idname (return bpy.ops.tks.delete_tag_item()), replacing the original target bpy.ops.tks.roadmap_remove_tag when the roadmap subsystem was removed. Recursion overflowed Blender's native C stack before any Python RecursionError could surface, so deleting any tag — most visibly an OUTPUT-category "rule" tag — silently terminated the process. Replaced the recursive self-call with an inline single-tag deletion that mirrors the batch-delete branch already in the same execute(): walk lib.categories for info['category_type'], select cat.tags (or cat.groups[<info['group_name']>].tags for grouped tags), target_collection.remove(info['tag_index']), clamp cat.active_tag_index, sync_tag_tree(context). See doc/troubleshooting/tag_delete_self_recursion_crash.md.

    [0.7.4] - 2026-05-20¶

    Added¶

    1. Camera Visibility Automation — only the active VL's camera is visible, hands-free. A new automation under Preferences → Workflow → Automations → Camera Visibility Automation keeps the outliner and viewport clean across view-layer switches. The master toggle activates the behavior; three granular sub-flags configure it: Show Assigned Camera clears hide_viewport, hide_render, and the per-VL eye icon on the cascade-resolved camera every time the view layer changes — even if the user had manually hidden it. Hide Other Cameras stamps the same three flags TRUE on every other CAMERA object in the active scene, so non-assigned cameras disappear from outliner, viewport, and render. Affect Containing Collection (nested under Show Assigned) additionally unhides the camera's direct host LayerCollection — clearing exclude (the Exclude-from-View-Layer checkbox), LayerCollection.hide_viewport (per-VL eye), and Collection.hide_viewport (global monitor icon). The host-reveal is bounded to one collection and never walks up the ancestor chain, so a hidden grandparent collection can keep the camera invisible by design (the user retains structural control). When the camera is linked into multiple collections, the first host whose ancestor chain is already fully visible wins; if none qualifies, the first host found is used. The whole feature is hooked into the cascade hot-path right after scene.camera = camera, short-circuits with zero cost when the master toggle is off, and persists across Blender restarts via addon prefs autosave. A Reset Camera Visibility operator clears all addon-stamped hide flags on every camera in the active scene without flipping any toggle — useful when you want to peek and then let the next VL switch re-isolate.
    2. Master toggle mirrored in the Takes Tree Settings popover. A new Camera Visibility row in the existing popover (above Previews) binds directly to the prefs master toggle, so you can switch the automation on or off from the same place you adjust Collection Visibility — no detour through Preferences. The granular sub-flags stay in prefs (set up once and leave them); the popover stays minimal. When the master toggle is on, the popover also surfaces the Reset button.
    3. Single-click cascade picker — list-at-cursor for every cascade icon. Plain left-click on an inline Action / World / Camera / Compositor / Output Rule icon now opens a native popup_menu at the cursor with the sorted list of available items (compositor node trees, world datablocks, scene cameras, automation-rule tags, etc.). The currently-assigned item is rendered depressed for at-a-glance feedback; clicking any item assigns and auto-closes the popup. Above the list, the popup shows (Clear), Create New (where a tier-specific _new operator exists — auto-assigns the freshly created datablock to the target via the picker's stashed context), and Rename '' (when an assignment exists and the underlying datablock is renameable). Modifier scheme: Shift+click still opens the existing full popover (rules + presets + push-to-selected + inherited source); Alt+click / Shift+Alt+click still clear / cascade-clear as before. Camera at VL level: the existing "select the assigned camera in viewport" gesture moved from Shift+click to Ctrl+Shift+click to free Shift for the full popover, matching the other props. Implemented as a generic _picker.py module (TKS_MT_CascadePicker, TKS_OT_SetCascadeProp, cascade_picker_invoke) that the four other props route through; Compositor keeps its dedicated TKS_MT_CompositorPicker since it was the proof-of-concept. The popup uses Blender's native menu chrome rather than an addon-rendered invoke_popup, so it visually matches stock dropdowns. The rename dialog is launched via a dedicated tks.picker_rename_deferred op because invoking invoke_props_dialog directly from a popup_menu callback dispatches unreliably; the wrapper replicates tks.casic_rename's rename + casic-string-update logic so the dispatch chain is one hop deep.
    4. Cascade Overrides popover redesign — inline editors instead of stacked floating popovers. The … overflow popover (shown for rows where icons are collapsed into the single chevron button) now mirrors the inline icon row: one flat icon per enabled cascade prop with the same active/dim/alert states, in the same canonical order. Click an icon to expand its editor inline within the popover (no second floating popup). For Action / World / Camera / Output Rule the inline editor calls the corresponding sub-popover operator's draw() via a duck-type wrapper, so the picker / rule / preset / push-to-selected widgets render natively without re-implementing each editor. Compositor uses the shared popover_draw helper directly. The active icon shows the pressed/blue background while its sub-popover is expanded. Alt+click any inner icon clears every assignment for that prop at this cascade level — direct value, rule, and preset together (Output Rule also wipes all five preset fields). Icons pinned outside collapse are excluded from the popover (they live inline on the row); the popover gates on tks_show_X AND NOT tks_pin_X to avoid duplicating pinned icons.
    5. "Never" collapse mode in Tree Design popover. Third option alongside Dynamic and Always on the Collapse row. When Never is active, right-side icons never collapse into the overflow chevron regardless of panel width — the user keeps full inline control at any list width. The Pin Outside Collapse box grays out in this mode since pinning has no effect when nothing overflows. Default stays Dynamic; the existing two-button row layout becomes a three-button row (Dynamic | Always | Never) so muscle memory for Dynamic and Always is preserved.
    6. Right-click context menu for takes-tree rows. Ctrl+RightMouse on a row in the 3D View N-panel opens a context menu with a header naming the active row (VL: green, SG: Shot 01, etc.) and a Show Overrides… entry that fires the cascade overrides popover for that row. Plain RightMouse was attempted first but is consumed by higher-priority Blender keymaps (UI button context menus, 3D-View RMB select), so Ctrl is added to claim an otherwise-unbound slot. The wrapper operator is poll-guarded on area.type == 'VIEW_3D' AND region.type == 'UI' AND active takes row exists, so the binding doesn't fire elsewhere in Blender's N-panels. The same menu is the natural place to grow other row-level actions later (Clear All Overrides, Copy / Paste Settings, etc.).
    7. Workflow > Automations preferences split into collapsible categories. The flat list of ~10 automation toggles is now grouped under six TRIA-expandable boxes — Rest State, Actions, Cameras, World, Previews, Render Presets — matching the box-and-triangle pattern used by Interface > Column Visibility. Each header is the same draw_collapsible_section helper the rest of the addon uses, so the look is native Blender (icon + title row inside a layout.box(), indented content column on expand). Six new expand_auto_* BoolProperty annotations on LoggingPropsMixin persist the collapse state to the addon prefs; default is collapsed. The Cameras box also gets a nested-indent treatment for the Camera Visibility master toggle and its three sub-flags (Show Assigned Camera → Affect Containing Collection; Hide Other Cameras), so the sub-rows visually read as children of the master via a row + separator(factor=PREFS_INDENT) + column indent helper.
    8. Workflow > Sync preferences mirror the same categorised layout. Viewport Tool Settings is now a collapsible category (single one today; Timeline / Autokey sync land as additional collapsibles in the same pattern). Inside, the master Enable Viewport Sync toggle sits at the top with the seven mirror sub-flags (Transform / Snap / Proportional / Mirror / Auto-Merge / Lock Object Mode / UV) indented one level beneath via the same indent helper used in Automations > Cameras. The two informational labels ("Mirror these across all scenes:", "Last-write-wins: …") have been removed — the per-toggle descriptions already convey the same intent. One new expand_sync_viewport BoolProperty.
    9. Compositor picker plain-click popup is sized to the content with an inline search field. Replaces bpy.ops.wm.search_single_menu (which has a fixed Blender-internal width that's too wide for short comp lists). New TKS_OT_CompositorSearchPopup opens via window_manager.invoke_popup(width=N) where N is computed at invoke time from the longest comp name (clamped 180–420 px) so a single-char name doesn't shrink the popup unreadably and a 100-char name doesn't blow past the screen. Top of the popup is a prop_search-style filter field (magnifying-glass icon, bound to WindowManager.tks_comp_picker_filter); below it, alphabetically-sorted COMPOSITING node groups render as emboss=False borderless rows so they read as list items rather than buttons. The active comp is drawn depress=True; the Clear action sits as a borderless footer row below a horizontal line separator. Filter text resets every time the popup opens.
    10. N-Panel warning when the active .blend was saved by a different addon MAJOR.MINOR — surfaces the "already-fixed bug reappears after addon update" failure mode. A save_pre handler stamps scene["tks_addon_version"] with the current ADDON_VERSION on every scene; a load_post handler reads the active scene back, compares MAJOR.MINOR (patch bumps stay silent), and sets wm.tks_cache_stale / wm.tks_cache_stale_from accordingly. On mismatch a PACKAGE icon toggle joins the warns row at the top-right of the N-Panel, alert-styled exactly like the other warning toggles and gated by the same mutual-exclusivity callback (_warn_props). Clicking it expands a Cache Version Mismatch subpanel below the nav bar — header row, info box with the offending version string, and a Rebuild Cache & Reload Addon action button. The button clears every in-memory cache the addon owns (rest_state.cache.invalidate_all, rest_cache.clear_cache, preset_cache.clear_caches, preset_engine.invalidate_preset_cache, panel.invalidate_nav_warnings), re-stamps the active scene, force-redraws, then schedules bpy.ops.preferences.addon_disable → addon_enable on a 0.1 s bpy.app.timers callback so the addon tears itself down past the operator return without ripping out the operator class mid-execute. Cache reset alone had been observed to leave the takes tree in a broken state, so the reload is bundled into the fix rather than offered as a separate optional step. The addon's unregister() already calls purge_modules(), so sys.modules is wiped before re-enable for a clean re-import. The stamp lives in a Scene IDProperty (not a registered StringProperty on a PropertyGroup) because IDProps survive PG schema changes — which is exactly the churn the stamp is meant to detect, so storing the stamp in a PG would be circular.

    Changed¶

    1. Cascade icon brightness now reflects every assignment type at every tier. Previously the inline icons used per-tier checks that were inconsistent — Camera at VL/VLG/VLV/SG/SCENE/GLOBAL was missing the *_camera_rule branch; SG/VLG world was missing tks_world_preset. After this pass, every cascade icon brightens when ANY of (direct value / rule / preset) is set, with the right tier-prefix (tks_global_* at Global, tks_scene_* for Scene presets, tks_* elsewhere). The cascade_queries.scene_has_camera() and global_has_camera() helpers now include the previously-missing tks_camera_rule / tks_global_camera_rule checks too.
    2. Overflow … chevron brightness now reflects only the icons that live in the popover. Previously the chevron lit up for any assignment on the row, even ones pinned outside collapse (where the pinned icon already showed its own bright state). Added an any_unpinned_active(wm, has_dict) helper in tree_layout_calc.py and updated all five tier any_active blocks (Global / SG / Scene / VLG / VL / VLV) to gate each contribution by NOT tks_pin_X, so a fully-pinned-outside row whose only assignments live on pinned icons no longer keeps the chevron lit.

    Fixed¶

    1. Addon no longer writes to Blender's user keyconfig — full non-interference with other addons and user customs. v0.7.3 stopped the Nav and Render Scope pies from polluting user kc, but the Keyframe pies on I / Alt+I still ran keymap_items.new() on wm.keyconfigs.user.keymaps['Window'] because Blender 5.x's Window/EMPTY keymap dispatch is unreliable for custom operator entries in addon kc alone. That bootstrap created is_user_defined=True entries in the Window keymap, and Blender's "rebuild user keyconfig on addon enable" pass on every cold restart drops all is_user_defined=True kmis in addon-touched keymaps — collateral damage to any other addon's user-kc overrides or user shortcuts that happen to live in Window. The keyframe pies now register in wm.keyconfigs.addon only, matching the rest of the addon. Active-flag sync on Blender's auto-mirror entry still happens (modifying an existing kmi doesn't change is_user_defined), so cold-start dispatch works. Trade-off: if Blender's auto-mirror doesn't sustain a custom-operator kmi across an in-session Reload Addon action (it sustains wm.call_menu_pie reliably but not tks.invoke_keyframe_pie), the keyframe pies may stop firing until the next full Blender restart. Accepted in favour of a clean user keymap — the addon is now a citizen that only touches its own keyconfig.
    2. Foreign-write and continuous-state instrumentation in the keymap-audit module. Used to bisect the non-interference fix. A trace_foreign_write() chokepoint logs [FOREIGN-WRITE] whenever the addon mutates a kmi outside the tks.* / wm.call_menu_pie namespace (only the intentional native-I / Alt+I deactivations should trigger this in normal operation). A bpy.app.timers periodic monitor at 2.5 s emits [AUDIT-DIFF] periodic-tick lines when keyconfig state changes between register / save / load boundaries, catching mutations from pref toggles or sibling-addon writes that aren't already wrapped by an audit phase. Both gated by the UI:HOTKEYS debug topic — useful for any future regression report.
    3. Group-level Compositor "Create New" no longer crashes with a TypeError. TKS_OT_GroupCompositorNew.execute() called find_scene_group(master, group_name) — a 2-arg call to a 1-arg function (find_scene_group(scene) looks up the SG that contains a given scene, not by name). Pre-existing bug that was only reachable via the new Create-from-picker entry on Scene Group rows; replaced with an explicit name lookup over get_scene_groups().
    4. Compositor picker classes were imported but never registered. TKS_MT_CompositorPicker and TKS_OT_SetCascadeCompositor were listed in panels/popovers/__init__.py::_misc_classes, but that file's register() is not in the addon's master register chain — the canonical class list lives in panels/context/_class_registry.py, which didn't include them. Net effect: clicking the compositor cascade icon opened a wm.search_single_menu against a menu idname that didn't exist in RNA, producing an empty popup. Both classes (plus the new TKS_OT_CompositorSearchPopup wrapper) are now in _class_registry.py's imports and classes list, and re-exported from panels/context_popovers.py so the import chain is consistent. The picker now actually lists the compositor node groups.
    5. tks_comp_picker_target_type WindowManager property moved above the class-registration loop in panels/context/__init__.py::register(). Previously sat after the for cls in classes: loop, so a failure mid-loop left the popover operator alive (since some operators register from a different module's classes list) but the property unbound — manifesting as AttributeError: 'WindowManager' object has no attribute 'tks_comp_picker_target_type' on the next compositor picker invoke. Moved alongside the related tks_comp_filtered collection so a class-loop hiccup can never strand it again. Defensive change; the underlying class-registration failure is fixed separately by entry #4.
    6. Camera Visibility automation now fires on group-tier camera assignments. VL Group / Scene Group / VL Version tks_camera StringProperty annotations have no update= callback by design — assigning a camera via the picker at one of those tiers used to silently write the value with no cascade refire, so the Camera Visibility hook (which lives inside apply_overrides()) never ran until the next VL switch. The generic picker setter TKS_OT_SetCascadeProp.execute() now explicitly calls apply_overrides(prop_filter=CascadeProperty.CAMERA) whenever prop_type == 'CAMERA'. Idempotent for VL / Scene / Global tiers (those already refire via their own update= callbacks), bulletproof for the group tiers that don't.
    7. Cascade icons (the red broken-state badge in particular) refresh instantly after a picker assignment. The icon-state cache _vl_cascade_cache in panels/context/draw_layers.py was only invalidated by the Scene / VL / Global update= callbacks (via _invalidate_and_redraw()) plus the ~200 ms context sync timer. Assigning at SG / VLG / VLV tiers — which don't have update callbacks — left the stale entry in place; the icon kept its old (often red/broken) color until the next sync tick. TKS_OT_SetCascadeProp.execute() now calls invalidate_vl_cascade_cache() plus signal_redraw() after every picker assignment regardless of prop type, since all four pickers (ACTION / WORLD / CAMERA / OUTPUT_RULE) share the same icon-state cache.
    8. Active takes-tree row no longer jumps to the last item after a cascade picker assignment. Assigning a value through the generic picker setter could leave wm.tks_all_viewlayers_index pointing somewhere unexpected — most visibly with ACTION assignments where the property write triggers depsgraph.update() + a context-sync-driven structural rebuild whose selected-key lookup occasionally mis-resolves. The picker click is meant to set a value on the row the user clicked, never to move the selection. TKS_OT_SetCascadeProp.execute() now snapshots the active tree index before setattr, runs the cascade refire + cache invalidation + redraw signal, and restores the saved index if it drifted (bounds-checked against the possibly-rebuilt collection, so we don't fight the system when the row genuinely vanished). Defensive — fixes the symptom for all four picker prop types (ACTION / WORLD / CAMERA / OUTPUT_RULE) regardless of which sync path is shuffling the index underneath.
    9. Scene / VL / VLG / VLV camera picker only shows cameras linked to the target scene, so the icon never stays red after a "successful" assignment. Previously the camera picker listed every CAMERA object in the file via _PICKER_CONFIG['CAMERA'].collection_fn. If the user picked a camera that lived only in another scene's collection hierarchy, the cascade engine's per-scene name in scene.objects validation in apply_overrides() (core/cascade.py:500-523) silently auto-cleared the assignment — the user saw the value briefly in the picker, then watched the cascade icon stay red because there genuinely was no usable camera at any resolved tier afterwards. New _camera_collection_fn(context) reads the picker's stashed tks_picker_scene_name + tks_picker_target_type and pre-filters to cameras in scene.objects when the target is scene-bound (Scene / VL / VLG / VLV). Scene-agnostic tiers (GLOBAL, SG) still see the full list because their cascade fans out to many scenes; the per-scene validation correctly happens at apply time there. The cascade's silent auto-clear safety net remains for stale assignments loaded from older .blend files or external scripts.

    [0.7.2] - 2026-05-13¶

    Added¶

    1. Keyframe pie menus on I and Alt+I — both off by default. Two opt-in pies. The Keyframe Pie (I) covers insert/set actions (Set as Rest Default, Insert at Rest State, Snap to Rest, Snap All to Rest, Insert Keyframe (Native)), and the Clear Pie (Alt+I) covers clear/remove actions (Clear Current Keyframe, Unset Rest Key (Channel), Unset Entire Rest Slot, Clear All Keyframes (Object), Clear All Rest Keys (VL), Delete Keyframe (Native)). Each pie has its own 8-slot configurator under Preferences → Workflow → Pie Menu with mutual-exclusion and reset workflow matching the Navigation and F12 pies. Enable each master toggle independently; until you do, I and Alt+I behave exactly like stock Blender.
    2. Pie hotkeys are now rebindable from the configurator. The center cell of every pie configurator (Navigation, F12 Render, Keyframe, Clear) is a live hotkey button — click it and Blender's "press a key" prompt captures a new key + modifier combo. Want to keep native I behavior and put the Keyframe Pie on a different key? Click the center cell and press your preferred chord. The same widget works for the Ctrl+Shift+C navigation pie and the F12 render pie. A reset icon (↩) sits glued to the hotkey field as a connected sibling button — one click restores the built-in default (Ctrl+Shift+C, F12, I, Alt+I) with a "Reset hotkey to default" tooltip. The whole rebind widget is centered between the W and E slot dropdowns and falls back to a static label when the pie's master toggle is off (no keymap entry to edit yet).
    3. Hotkeys panel lists all four pie shortcuts. The Navigation, F12 Render, Keyframe, and Clear pie entries now appear inline in Preferences → Workflow → Hotkeys alongside the other Takes shortcuts, so you can review or rebind every pie from one place with the standard Blender keymap-editor controls (expand row, change modifiers, restore default).
    4. Editor Scope for the keyframe pies covers every keyframe-capable editor. Per-editor checkboxes under Preferences → Workflow → Pie Menu → Editor Scope let you opt the pies into the 3D Viewport, Properties, Graph Editor, Dope Sheet, NLA Editor, Shader Editor, Image Editor, Movie Clip Editor, Video Sequencer, and Outliner. The wrapper routes per context.area.type and falls back to the editor's native I / Alt+I (anim.keyframe_insert, anim.keyframe_insert_button, graph.keyframe_insert, clip.keyframe_insert, …) when an editor's toggle is off, so disabled editors keep native behavior.
    5. Hover-aware slot visibility. Outside the 3D Viewport, hover-dependent slots (anything that needs a specific property — Set/Insert at Rest, Snap to Rest, Clear Current Keyframe, Unset Rest Key (Channel), Insert/Delete Keyframe (Native)) only appear when the cursor is over a keyframable value. Empty canvas hides them and leaves the slot direction as a separator, so muscle memory still works for the 8 directions. The 3D Viewport always shows every slot — selection-based actions don't need hover.
    6. Three new Rest State operators. Unset Rest Key (Channel) removes a single fcurve's channel for the active property, Unset Entire Rest Slot removes the active object's slot from the Rest State action, and Clear All Rest Keys (VL) walks every object in the active view layer and clears their rest slots. All three appear as slot choices in the Clear Pie.
    7. Viewport tool settings now sync across scenes. A new Workflow → Sync → Viewport Tool Settings section lets you mirror selected 3D viewport tool settings — transform orientation + pivot + Affect-Only toggles, snap settings, proportional editing, mirror, auto-merge, lock-object-mode, UV — across every scene as you change them. Last-write-wins: any scene's change to a synced setting propagates to all the others. Each group has its own toggle, gated by a master Enable Viewport Sync switch (off by default). The msgbus subscriptions are only armed while the master is on.
    8. Auto-clearing the Scene World on an empty cascade is now optional. A new Auto-clear World when Unassigned toggle under Preferences → Workflow → Automations (on by default) controls whether scene.world gets wiped when no world is assigned anywhere in the Takes tree. With it off, the existing Scene World is preserved and the Cascade Drift warning surfaces persistently as None → <WorldName> to remind you to put a world into the tree (or accept the manual assignment).
    9. Apply Scene World to any cascade tier from the drift warning. The drift row for World now opens a tier-picker dropdown (Global / Scene Group / Scene / VL Group / View Layer / VL Version) — pick a tier and the active scene.world is written into that level's tks_world override. Tiers that don't apply for the active context (no Scene/VL Group beyond the default "Ungrouped", no active VL Version) are greyed out. Replaces the single-target Accept button for World drift; Accept still appears for Compositor drift.
    10. Undo can no longer silently destroy a manually-assigned Scene World. A new Skip World-Clear in Post-Undo Cascade required-core strategy (on by default, under Preferences → Workflow → Debug → Undo-Redo) makes the post-undo apply_overrides skip the world-clear branch entirely. Before this, undoing back to a state where no world was in the cascade tree would wipe scene.world on the very next post-undo cascade run — even if the user had assigned it outside the tree.

    Changed¶

    1. The Inspector Watchlist keeps a stable height when it's empty. The list and its sidebar buttons (Add / Remove / Settings / Find Slot) now always render; the empty-state info message appears as a row in the stats slot above the list instead of replacing the whole list with an info box. The panel no longer jumps in height the moment the last watched object is removed.

    Fixed¶

    1. Pie hotkey rebinds now persist across every routine pref change. Earlier 0.7.2 builds rebuilt the pie keymap entries on every Editor Scope checkbox flip, master toggle round-trip, and addon reload — wiping any custom key the user had bound via the configurator's center hotkey button or via Blender's keymap editor. _register_keymap() is now idempotent across all three pies (Navigation, F12 Render, I + Alt+I) — it preserves existing kmi entries when found and only flips the active flag to match master state. Per-editor toggles and slot dropdown changes no longer touch the keymap layer at all (the wrapper operator reads prefs dynamically). Full keymap teardown only happens on addon unregister.
    2. New codebase audit catches scope-crossing writes early. Part J of the codebase stats (doc/reports/codebase_stats.md) now scans every Python file for writes to wm.keyconfigs.user and wm.keyconfigs.default and lists them grouped by severity. Lines tagged with a # SCOPE_OK: <reason> comment are exempt and still listed for review; anything unjustified deducts from the Health Score. The 17 legitimate user-keyconfig writes in 0.7.2 (Blender 5.x dispatch workaround, master-toggle reversible flips, full-teardown removes on unregister) all carry the marker now, so the audit reads 0 unjustified scope crossings.
    3. Pie menu keymaps no longer crash Blender on per-editor toggle. Flipping a checkbox in Editor Scope (or any path that re-runs pie keymap registration) could trigger an EXCEPTION_ACCESS_VIOLATION deep inside rna_KeyMap_item_remove → BLI_findindex when a stored kmi C-pointer had been freed by Blender between cycles. The unregister path now walks each keyconfig fresh and matches entries by idname + properties, so it never dereferences a stale pointer. The same hardening is applied to the Navigation, F12 Render Scope, Global Shortcuts, Tag Groups, and Context panel keymap teardowns.
    4. Ctrl+Shift+C navigation pie and F12 render pie fire reliably in Blender 5.x. Both pies registered only in the addon keyconfig and relied on Blender to mirror entries into the user keyconfig — which Blender 5.x doesn't do reliably, so dispatch silently failed even though DIAG showed entries active=True. Each pie now registers in both keyconfigs explicitly, the same fix used for the new I-key pies.
    5. The Post-Undo Cascade Ping no longer silently aborts on scenes without a compositor node tree. A null scene.node_tree access raised a non-fatal exception that bailed the entire ping mid-scan, so any datablock not yet visited never had its cascade rebuilt. The access is now guarded so the ping continues with the rest of the scan.
    6. The render-window-close watcher fires reliably during undo bursts again. The mutation-skip guard added in 0.7.1 broke the post-undo cascade ping — it relied on this timer firing promptly during undo. The guard is removed; a K5_EXEMPT code comment plus a project audit note keep it from being reintroduced.
    7. The F12 Render Scope pie shows operator errors as status-bar messages instead of console tracebacks. When the inner batch render operator raises a RuntimeError via self.report({'ERROR'}, …) — e.g. "Save file before starting Batch Render!" — the pie's dispatcher now catches it and re-reports the message via the pie operator's own status bar.
    8. Clean Empty Slots & Actions has a combined operator, a preview dialog, and a safety pass. A single Clean Empty Slots & Actions runs both passes after showing a preview of what will be removed; an extra safety pass leaves fake-user-pinned actions and slots that are still referenced elsewhere alone.
    9. JIT rest action cleanup runs in the two merge branches that previously skipped it. Two specific just-in-time merge paths left their source actions behind without scheduling them for removal — they now follow the same cleanup schedule as every other branch, so orphan actions stop accumulating after long sessions.
    10. Preset capture covers Hydra Storm engine settings and the Output Time Stretching ratio. Render presets now save scene.hydra.* (visible under Render Properties → Hydra when the render engine is Hydra Storm — currently just Export Method). Output presets now save the Time Stretching Old / New frame-mapping ratio. Both were silently absent before.
    11. Accepting a Cascade Drift no longer crashes on World or Compositor. accept_drift was assigning a World / NodeTree datablock to vl.tks_world / vl.tks_compositor, both of which are StringProperty. The latent type-mismatch was masked by the old auto-clear-world behavior never producing a drift in the relevant case; with the world-clear toggle the drift becomes reachable. Accept now writes actual.name and clears with "" to match the property type.
    12. The Context tree view now repopulates on every file load, not only the first of a session. The _sync_timer fast-path gate is driven by module-level globals in panels/context/handlers.py (_sync_dirty/_context_sync_dirty/_last_fingerprint/_last_structure_key). They start True (first load populates) then flip False after the first sync. Being Python globals they survive File>Open, but the WM-backed tks_all_viewlayers collection is reset by the load (Load UI swaps in the file's WM) → empty collection + closed gate + no re-arm = blank tree. The structural fallback only re-arms on a scene/VL count change (a same-structure reload doesn't trip it) and World-stored group data doesn't reliably fire depsgraph_update_post on load — the exact gap _handle_undo_redo_sync already covers for undo/redo. Fix: new @persistent _handle_load_post_sync (file-load twin of the undo handler) re-arms both dirty flags, nulls _last_fingerprint/_last_structure_key, and busts TKS_UL_AllViewLayers._sg_cache_token / groups._vs_cache_token; registered/unregistered on bpy.app.handlers.load_post in panels/context/__init__.py. Tests: dev/tests/test_tree_load_refire.py (5 — flag re-arm, fingerprint/structure-key clear, load_post arg tolerance, registration). 543/543 headless. See doc/troubleshooting/tree_blank_after_second_file_load.md.
